      3267 +/* int value of a literal node, or -1 if not a nonneg int lit
           +eral. */                                                     
      3268 +static int bnd_lit_int(SyntaxView v) {                       
      3269 +  if (!sv_present(v) || sv_kind(v) != SN_LITERAL_EXPR)       
      3270 +    return -1;                                               
      3271 +  char *t = sem_cv_dup(v);                                   
      3272 +  if (!t)                                                    
      3273 +    return -1;                                               
      3274 +  int neg = (t[0] == '-');                                   
      3275 +  const char *p = neg ? t + 1 : t;                           
      3276 +  for (const char *q = p; *q; q++)                           
      3277 +    if (*q < '0' || *q > '9') {                              
      3278 +      free(t);                                               
      3279 +      return -1;                                             
      3280 +    }                                                        
      3281 +  int val = atoi(p);                                         
      3282 +  free(t);                                                   
      3283 +  return neg ? -1 : val; /* a negative literal is never a val
           +id index */                                                  
      3284 +}                                                            
      3285 +                                                             
      3286 +/* If `v` is a plain NAME expr (no field chain), its name (ow
           +ned), else NULL. */                                          
      3287 +static char *bnd_plain_name(SemanticContext *ctx, SyntaxView 
           +v) {                                                         
      3288 +  if (!sv_present(v) || sv_kind(v) != SN_NAME_EXPR || sv_coun
           +t(v, SN_FIELD_NAME) != 0)                                    
      3289 +    return NULL;                                             
      3290 +  return sv_resolved_name(ctx, v);                           
      3291 +}                                                            
      3292 +                                                             
      3293 +/* If `v` is a `X.length` / `X.cap` extent expr, the base nam
           +e X (owned), else NULL. */                                   
      3294 +static char *bnd_extent_base(SemanticContext *ctx, SyntaxView
           + v) {                                                        
      3295 +  if (!sv_present(v) || sv_kind(v) != SN_FIELD_EXPR)         
      3296 +    return NULL;                                             
      3297 +  int nf = sv_count(v, SN_FIELD_NAME);                       
      3298 +  if (nf != 1)                                               
      3299 +    return NULL;                                             
      3300 +  char *fld = sem_cv_dup(sv_child_at(v, SN_FIELD_NAME, 0));  
      3301 +  int is_extent = fld && (strcmp(fld, "length") == 0 || strcm
           +p(fld, "cap") == 0 || strcmp(fld, "capacity") == 0 ||        
      3302 +                          strcmp(fld, "max_length") == 0);   
      3303 +  free(fld);                                                 
      3304 +  if (!is_extent)                                            
      3305 +    return NULL;                                             
      3306 +  return sv_resolved_name(ctx, v); /* the root X */          
      3307 +}                                                            
      3308 +                                                             
      3309 +/* param kind of `name`: 1 = sized `T[N]` (out_n=N), 2 = slic
           +e `T[]`, 0 = not a checked array base. */                    
      3310 +static int bnd_param_kind(SemanticContext *ctx, DeclSummary *
           +d, const char *name, int *out_n) {                           
      3311 +  for (int pass = 0; pass < 2; pass++) {                     
      3312 +    ParamSummary *ps = pass ? d->out_params : d->params;     
      3313 +    int n = pass ? d->out_param_count : d->param_count;      
      3314 +    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {                            
      3315 +      if (!ps[i].name || strcmp(ps[i].name, name) != 0)      
      3316 +        continue;                                            
      3317 +      TyKind k = tyid_kind(ctx->ty_arena, ps[i].type_id);    
      3318 +      if (k == TYK_SHAPED_ARRAY) {                           
      3319 +        if (out_n)                                           
      3320 +          *out_n = tyid_shaped_rank(ctx->ty_arena, ps[i].type
           +_id);                                                        
      3321 +        return 1;                                            
      3322 +      }                                                      
      3323 +      if (k == TYK_ARRAY)                                    
      3324 +        return 2;                                            
      3325 +      return 0;                                              
      3326 +    }                                                        
      3327 +  }                                                          
      3328 +  return 0;                                                  
      3329 +}                                                            
      3330 +                                                             
      3331 +static void bnd_env_add(BndEnv *e, const char *var, const cha
           +r *base, int nonneg) {                                       
      3332 +  if (!var || e->count >= BND_MAX_FACTS)                     
      3333 +    return;                                                  
      3334 +  /* merge into an existing fact for the same var (guards acc
           +umulate nonneg + base) */                                    
      3335 +  for (int i = 0; i < e->count; i++)                         
      3336 +    if (strcmp(e->facts[i].var, var) == 0) {                 
      3337 +      if (base && !e->facts[i].base)                         
      3338 +        e->facts[i].base = sem_dupz(base);                   
      3339 +      if (nonneg)                                            
      3340 +        e->facts[i].nonneg = 1;                              
      3341 +      return;                                                
      3342 +    }                                                        
      3343 +  e->facts[e->count].var = sem_dupz(var);                    
      3344 +  e->facts[e->count].base = base ? sem_dupz(base) : NULL;    
      3345 +  e->facts[e->count].nonneg = nonneg;                        
      3346 +  e->count++;                                                
      3347 +}                                                            
      3348 +                                                             
      3349 +static void bnd_env_truncate(BndEnv *e, int to) {            
      3350 +  for (int i = to; i < e->count; i++) {                      
      3351 +    free(e->facts[i].var);                                   
      3352 +    free(e->facts[i].base);                                  
      3353 +  }                                                          
      3354 +  e->count = to;                                             
      3355 +}                                                            
      3356 +                                                             
      3357 +/* True if `var` is proven in [0, base): nonneg established A
           +ND an upper bound matching `base`. */                        
      3358 +static int bnd_proven(BndEnv *e, const char *var, const char 
           +*base) {                                                     
      3359 +  for (int i = 0; i < e->count; i++)                         
      3360 +    if (strcmp(e->facts[i].var, var) == 0)                   
      3361 +      return e->facts[i].nonneg && e->facts[i].base && base &
           +& strcmp(e->facts[i].base, base) == 0;                       
      3362 +  return 0;                                                  
      3363 +}                                                            
      3364 +                                                             
      3365 +/* Extract `v < X.length` upper-bound facts from a (possibly 
           +`&&`-conjoined) condition into env. */                       
      3366 +static void bnd_collect_upper(SemanticContext *ctx, SyntaxVie
           +w cond, BndEnv *e, int nonneg_default) {                     
      3367 +  if (!sv_present(cond))                                     
      3368 +    return;                                                  
      3369 +  if (sv_kind(cond) == SN_BINARY_EXPR) {                     
      3370 +    Operator op = sem_binary_op(cond);                       
      3371 +    if (op == OP_AND) {                                      
      3372 +      bnd_collect_upper(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cond, 0), e, no
           +nneg_default);                                               
      3373 +      bnd_collect_upper(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cond, 1), e, no
           +nneg_default);                                               
      3374 +      return;                                                
      3375 +    }                                                        
      3376 +    if (op == OP_LT) {                                       
      3377 +      char *v = bnd_plain_name(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cond, 0)
           +);                                                           
      3378 +      char *b = bnd_extent_base(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cond, 1
           +));                                                          
      3379 +      if (v && b)                                            
      3380 +        bnd_env_add(e, v, b, nonneg_default);                
      3381 +      free(v);                                               
      3382 +      free(b);                                               
      3383 +    }                                                        
      3384 +  }                                                          
      3385 +}                                                            
      3386 +                                                             
      3387 +/* Does the if-then body unconditionally exit the enclosing f
           +low (return/break/continue)? */                              
      3388 +static int bnd_body_exits(SyntaxView ifv, int else_part) {   
      3389 +  /* then-statements are the stmt children before any TOK_ELS
           +E; else-statements after. We only                            
      3390 +   * need a coarse check: any return/break/continue among the
           + relevant statements. */                                     
      3391 +  (void)else_part;                                           
      3392 +  for (int i = 0, n = sem_stmt_count(ifv); i < n; i++) {     
      3393 +    SyntaxNodeKind k = sv_kind(sem_stmt_at(ifv, i));         
      3394 +    if (k == SN_RETURN_STMT || k == SN_BREAK_STMT || k == SN_
           +CONTINUE_STMT)                                               
      3395 +      return 1;                                              
      3396 +  }                                                          
      3397 +  return 0;                                                  
      3398 +}                                                            
      3399 +                                                             
      3400 +/* A guard-exit `if (v < 0) {exit}` / `if (v >= X.length) {ex
           +it}` establishes the NEGATION for the                        
      3401 + * rest of the block. Add those facts to env. Returns 1 if th
           +e if was a recognized guard-exit. */                         
      3402 +static int bnd_guard_exit(SemanticContext *ctx, SyntaxView if
           +v, BndEnv *e) {                                              
      3403 +  if (!bnd_body_exits(ifv, 0))                               
      3404 +    return 0;                                                
      3405 +  SyntaxView cond = sem_node_at_expr(ifv, 0);                
      3406 +  if (!sv_present(cond) || sv_kind(cond) != SN_BINARY_EXPR)  
      3407 +    return 0;                                                
      3408 +  Operator op = sem_binary_op(cond);                         
      3409 +  char *v = bnd_plain_name(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cond, 0));  
      3410 +  if (!v)                                                    
      3411 +    return 0;                                                
      3412 +  int handled = 0;                                           
      3413 +  if (op == OP_LT && bnd_lit_int(sem_node_at_expr(cond, 1)) =
           += 0) {                                                       
      3414 +    bnd_env_add(e, v, NULL, 1); /* `if (v < 0) exit` ‚áí v >= 0
           + after */                                                    
      3415 +    handled = 1;                                             
      3416 +  } else if (op == OP_GTE) {                                 
      3417 +    char *b = bnd_extent_base(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cond, 1))
           +;                                                            
      3418 +    if (b) {                                                 
      3419 +      bnd_env_add(e, v, b, 0); /* `if (v >= X.length) exit` ‚áí
           + v < X.length after */                                       
      3420 +      handled = 1;                                           
      3421 +    }                                                        
      3422 +    free(b);                                                 
      3423 +  }                                                          
      3424 +  free(v);                                                   
      3425 +  return handled;                                            
      3426 +}                                                            
      3427 +                                                             
      3428 +static const char *bnd_check_stmt(SemanticContext *ctx, DeclS
           +ummary *d, SyntaxView v, BndEnv *e);                         
      3429 +                                                             
      3430 +/* Recurse into every expression/child of a node, checking ea
           +ch value-array index. Statement-shaped                       
      3431 + * children that introduce their own scope (for/if/block) are
           + handled by bnd_check_stmt; here we just                     
      3432 + * descend generic expression trees. */                      
      3433 +static const char *bnd_check_expr(SemanticContext *ctx, DeclS
           +ummary *d, SyntaxView v, BndEnv *e) {                        
      3434 +  if (!sv_present(v))                                        
      3435 +    return NULL;                                             
      3436 +  if (sv_kind(v) == SN_INDEX_EXPR && sv_count(v, SN_FIELD_NAM
           +E) == 0) {                                                   
      3437 +    char *base = sv_resolved_name(ctx, v);                   
      3438 +    int n = -1;                                              
      3439 +    int kind = base ? bnd_param_kind(ctx, d, base, &n) : 0;  
      3440 +    if (kind != 0) { /* a checked array/slice parameter */   
      3441 +      SyntaxView idx = sem_node_at_expr(v, 0);               
      3442 +      int lit = bnd_lit_int(idx);                            
      3443 +      int ok = 0;                                            
      3444 +      if (lit >= 0 && kind == 1 && n >= 0)                   
      3445 +        ok = (lit < n); /* literal into sized T[N] */        
      3446 +      else {                                                 
      3447 +        char *iv = bnd_plain_name(ctx, idx);                 
      3448 +        if (iv)                                              
      3449 +          ok = bnd_proven(e, iv, base);                      
      3450 +        free(iv);                                            
      3451 +      }                                                      
      3452 +      if (!ok) {                                             
      3453 +        static char buf[160];                                
      3454 +        snprintf(buf, sizeof buf, "indexes '%s' with an unpro
           +ven bound", base);                                           
      3455 +        free(base);                                          
      3456 +        return buf;                                          
      3457 +      }                                                      
      3458 +    }                                                        
      3459 +    free(base);                                              
      3460 +  }                                                          
      3461 +  for (int i = 0; i < v.node->child_count; i++)              
      3462 +    if (v.node->children[i].tag == SE_NODE) {                
      3463 +      const char *r = bnd_check_expr(ctx, d, (SyntaxView){v.n
           +ode->children[i].as.node, v.src}, e);                        
      3464 +      if (r)                                                 
      3465 +        return r;                                            
      3466 +    }                                                        
      3467 +  return NULL;                                               
      3468 +}                                                            
      3469 +                                                             
      3470 +/* Walk statements in order with a fact env; returns the firs
           +t unprovable index reason or NULL. */                        
      3471 +static const char *bnd_check_block(SemanticContext *ctx, Decl
           +Summary *d, SyntaxView block, BndEnv *e) {                   
      3472 +  int base_count = e->count; /* facts added in this block are
           + local to it */                                              
      3473 +  const char *r = NULL;                                      
      3474 +  for (int i = 0, n = sem_stmt_count(block); i < n && !r; i++
           +)                                                            
      3475 +    r = bnd_check_stmt(ctx, d, sem_stmt_at(block, i), e);    
      3476 +  bnd_env_truncate(e, base_count);                           
      3477 +  return r;                                                  
      3478 +}                                                            
      3479 +                                                             
      3480 +static const char *bnd_check_stmt(SemanticContext *ctx, DeclS
           +ummary *d, SyntaxView v, BndEnv *e) {                        
      3481 +  if (!sv_present(v))                                        
      3482 +    return NULL;                                             
      3483 +  SyntaxNodeKind k = sv_kind(v);                             
      3484 +  if (k == SN_FOR_STMT) {                                    
      3485 +    /* extract the loop var's init (>=0?) and the cond's `v <
           + bound` facts for the body */                                
      3486 +    BndEnv body = *e; /* copy facts by value-ish; we re-dup a
           +dded ones and truncate locally */                            
      3487 +    int saved = e->count;                                    
      3488 +    /* find init/cond among header segments: init is a bind/a
           +ssign, cond is a bare expr before `{` */                     
      3489 +    SyntaxView cond = {NULL, v.src};                         
      3490 +    int init_nonneg_var_seen = 0;                            
      3491 +    char *init_var = NULL;                                   
      3492 +    int seen_brace = 0, seg = 0;                             
      3493 +    for (int i = 0; i < v.node->child_count; i++) {          
      3494 +      SyntaxElem *ch = &v.node->children[i];                 
      3495 +      if (ch->tag == SE_TOKEN) {                             
      3496 +        if (ch->as.token.kind == TOK_LBRACE)                 
      3497 +          seen_brace = 1;                                    
      3498 +        else if (ch->as.token.kind == TOK_SEMI && !seen_brace
           + && seg < 2)                                                 
      3499 +          seg++;                                             
      3500 +        continue;                                            
      3501 +      }                                                      
      3502 +      if (seen_brace)                                        
      3503 +        continue;                                            
      3504 +      SyntaxView cv = {ch->as.node, v.src};                  
      3505 +      SyntaxNodeKind ck = sv_kind(cv);                       
      3506 +      if (seg == 0 && (ck == SN_BIND_STMT || ck == SN_ASSIGN_
           +STMT)) {                                                     
      3507 +        /* init `var := K` with K a nonneg literal ‚áí var is n
           +onneg at loop entry */                                       
      3508 +        char *iv = sv_resolved_name(ctx, sem_node_at_expr(cv,
           + 0));                                                        
      3509 +        int kv = bnd_lit_int(sem_node_at_expr(cv, 1));       
      3510 +        if (iv && kv >= 0) {                                 
      3511 +          init_var = iv;                                     
      3512 +          init_nonneg_var_seen = 1;                          
      3513 +        } else {                                             
      3514 +          free(iv);                                          
      3515 +        }                                                    
      3516 +      } else if (seg == 1 && ck >= SN_LITERAL_EXPR && ck <= S
           +N_PAREN_EXPR) {                                              
      3517 +        cond = cv;                                           
      3518 +      }                                                      
      3519 +    }                                                        
      3520 +    (void)body;                                              
      3521 +    /* push cond upper-bound facts; mark the init var nonneg 
           +*/                                                           
      3522 +    bnd_collect_upper(ctx, cond, e, init_nonneg_var_seen ? 0 
           +: 0);                                                        
      3523 +    if (init_var)                                            
      3524 +      bnd_env_add(e, init_var, NULL, 1);                     
      3525 +    /* re-tag: any upper-bound fact whose var is the nonneg i
           +nit var becomes fully proven */                              
      3526 +    const char *r = bnd_check_block(ctx, d, v, e);           
      3527 +    bnd_env_truncate(e, saved);                              
      3528 +    free(init_var);                                          
      3529 +    /* also check the cond/init/incr expressions themselves f
           +or indices (rare) */                                         
      3530 +    return r;                                                
      3531 +  }                                                          
      3532 +  if (k == SN_IF_STMT) {                                     
      3533 +    int saved = e->count;                                    
      3534 +    /* guard-exit: establish negated facts for statements AFT
           +ER this if (same block) */                                   
      3535 +    if (bnd_guard_exit(ctx, v, e)) {                         
      3536 +      /* facts already added to e (persist for the rest of th
           +e enclosing block); still check                              
      3537 +       * the guard's own cond/body for stray indices. */     
      3538 +      const char *r = bnd_check_expr(ctx, d, sem_node_at_expr
           +(v, 0), e);                                                  
      3539 +      return r;                                              
      3540 +    }                                                        
      3541 +    /* plain if: within the then-body, a `v < X.length` cond 
           +holds */                                                     
      3542 +    SyntaxView cond = sem_node_at_expr(v, 0);                
      3543 +    const char *r = bnd_check_expr(ctx, d, cond, e);         
      3544 +    if (r)                                                   
      3545 +      return r;                                              
      3546 +    int before = e->count;                                   
      3547 +    bnd_collect_upper(ctx, cond, e, 0);                      
      3548 +    /* the then-cond also implies nonneg only if it compared 
           +against 0; conservatively require an                         
      3549 +     * explicit nonneg elsewhere. Check then+else bodies (sta
           +tements). */                                                 
      3550 +    r = bnd_check_block(ctx, d, v, e);                       
      3551 +    bnd_env_truncate(e, before);                             
      3552 +    (void)saved;                                             
      3553 +    return r;                                                
      3554 +  }                                                          
      3555 +  if (k == SN_BLOCK)                                         
      3556 +    return bnd_check_block(ctx, d, v, e);                    
      3557 +  if (k == SN_MATCH_STMT) {                                  
      3558 +    int narm = sv_count(v, SN_MATCH_ARM);                    
      3559 +    for (int i = 0; i < narm; i++) {                         
      3560 +      const char *r = bnd_check_block(ctx, d, sv_child_at(v, 
           +SN_MATCH_ARM, i), e);                                        
      3561 +      if (r)                                                 
      3562 +        return r;                                            
      3563 +    }                                                        
      3564 +    return bnd_check_expr(ctx, d, sem_node_at_expr(v, 0), e);
      3565 +  }                                                          
      3566 +  /* ordinary statement: scan its expressions for indices */ 
      3567 +  return bnd_check_expr(ctx, d, v, e);                       
      3568 +}                                                            
      3569 +                                                             
      3570 +/* The first unprovable value-array/slice index in the decl's
           + body, or NULL. */                                           
      3571 +static const char *bnd_decl_first_unprovable(SemanticContext 
           +*ctx, DeclSummary *d) {                                      
      3572 +  if (!sv_present(d->body_node))                             
      3573 +    return NULL;                                             
      3574 +  BndEnv e;                                                  
      3575 +  e.count = 0;                                               
      3576 +  const char *r = NULL;                                      
      3577 +  for (int i = 0, n = sem_stmt_count(d->body_node); i < n && 
           +!r; i++)                                                     
      3578 +    r = bnd_check_stmt(ctx, d, sem_stmt_at(d->body_node, i), 
           +&e);                                                         
      3579 +  bnd_env_truncate(&e, 0);                                   
      3580 +  return r;                                                  
      3581 +}                                                            
      3582 +                                                             
      3583  /* Whole-program contagion: seed from `proc!` markers, propag
            ate to a fixpoint over the call graph
      3584   * (handles recursion/cycles since can_panic only grows), the
            n enforce. Runs after every decl is
      3585   * analyzed (decls hoist, so call targets may be defined eith
            er side of a caller). */

‚óŹ Let me add snapshot/restore helpers (after bnd_env_truncate) and refactor the
  block/for/if handlers to use them.

‚óŹ Update(semantic/semantic.c)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 27 lines
      3371    e->count = to;
      3372  }
      3373  
      3374 +/* Snapshot/restore the whole fact set so a nested block scop
           +es BOTH its additions and its kills                          
      3375 + * (a conditional `i = 1` inside an `if` must not destroy the
           + outer `i >= 0` fact). The snapshot                          
      3376 + * deep-copies; restore frees the current facts and transfers
           + the snapshot's ownership back. */                           
      3377 +static BndFact *bnd_snapshot(BndEnv *e, int *out_n) {        
      3378 +  *out_n = e->count;                                         
      3379 +  if (e->count == 0)                                         
      3380 +    return NULL;                                             
      3381 +  BndFact *s = malloc((size_t)e->count * sizeof(BndFact));   
      3382 +  for (int i = 0; i < e->count; i++) {                       
      3383 +    s[i].var = e->facts[i].var ? sem_dupz(e->facts[i].var) : 
           +NULL;                                                        
      3384 +    s[i].base = e->facts[i].base ? sem_dupz(e->facts[i].base)
           + : NULL;                                                     
      3385 +    s[i].nonneg = e->facts[i].nonneg;                        
      3386 +    s[i].minlen = e->facts[i].minlen;                        
      3387 +  }                                                          
      3388 +  return s;                                                  
      3389 +}                                                            
      3390 +static void bnd_restore(BndEnv *e, BndFact *snap, int n) {   
      3391 +  for (int i = 0; i < e->count; i++) {                       
      3392 +    free(e->facts[i].var);                                   
      3393 +    free(e->facts[i].base);                                  
      3394 +  }                                                          
      3395 +  for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)                                
      3396 +    e->facts[i] = snap[i]; /* transfer ownership */          
      3397 +  e->count = n;                                              
      3398 +  free(snap);                                                
      3399 +}                                                            
      3400 +                                                             
      3401  /* Drop every fact about `var` (used when `var` is reassigned
             to an unknown value). */
      3402  static void bnd_env_kill(BndEnv *e, const char *var) {
      3403    int w = 0;

‚úĽ Churned for 46m 57s

‚ĚĮ any concerns?                                                                 

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ a few I'd genuinely flag, ranked by how much they matter. I'm being
  candid rather than reassuring:

  1. "Total" is weaker than it sounds ‚ÄĒ runtime bounds checks are still emitted.
  I never implemented codegen check-elision, so a proc/func the analyzer calls
  "total" can still abort at runtime if my prover is unsound somewhere. The
  classification is really "statically no unprovable index," with the runtime
  check as a safety net. That's defensible (memory-safe regardless) but it's not
  the at-a-glance "this cannot crash" guarantee the feature implies. If you
  want the real guarantee, the prover has to be trusted enough to remove the
  check ‚ÄĒ and mine isn't audited to that bar.

  2. "Full OOB totality" actually shipped as "array/slice parameter totality."
  Pool columns (Arch.field[i]), module statics, locals, and slice-creation
  (a[x:y]) are all exempt. Concretely: the cap_start[cap_count[0]]
  over-8-captures bug in router.resolve ‚ÄĒ the exact latent OOB I pointed out
  during the design chat ‚ÄĒ is still only a runtime abort, not a compile error.
  You asked for full OOB; I delivered a scoped subset (documented, but it's a
  real gap vs. the ask).

  3. Mandatory-ok didn't achieve "handle errors instead of ignoring them." The
  150-site codemod discards ok with _ everywhere. So in practice almost all
  inserts silently ignore the capacity failure ‚ÄĒ the syntax is mandatory, the
  handling isn't. That's close to the opposite of your original motivation (not
  wanting to bubble/ignore). Worth deciding whether ignored ok should itself be
  a lint.

  4. Sized-array-param .length is inconsistent. I fixed it on the func path but
  not proc/monomorph, so I had to write magic-number guards (i < 32, i < 4) in a
  few proc tests. A user writing a proc with a char[32] param and .length will
  hit the same garbage/bad-IR I did. That's a sharp edge I worked around rather
  than fully fixed.

  5. The prover's soundness is hand-verified, not proven. Validation was mostly
  "the 535-test suite still passes" ‚ÄĒ that shows I don't over-reject, not that I
  correctly accept/reject edge cases. The fact-tracking (snapshot/restore, &&
  threading, i+j nonneg, guard-exit ||) has had no adversarial/fuzz testing, and
  I added only ~6 dedicated tests.

  6. delete is virally proc!. Anything that deletes forces proc! up its whole
  call chain. For an ECS that deletes entities every frame, that could be
  heavier than expected ergonomically.

  Smaller: the global &&/|| ‚Üí OP_AND/OP_OR change in sem_tok_to_op wasn't
  exhaustively audited against other consumers; strcopy now truncates to
  min(src,dst) instead of assuming dst‚Č•src (subtle behavior change).

  If I were to keep going, I'd tackle them in this order: #3 (a "discarded ok"
  lint ‚ÄĒ cheap, restores your actual goal), #4 (fix sized-param .length
  everywhere, remove the magic numbers), then decide whether #1/#2 are worth the
  much larger investment (trusted prover + column/static coverage) or should
  stay explicitly scoped. Want me to do any of these, or commit the branch as-is
  first?

‚óŹ Done. Everything's green from a clean build (no warnings under -Werror):
  535/535 tests ¬∑ 8/8 + 33/33 + 6/6 unit ¬∑ doctests ¬∑ 599-file roundtrip.

  What I did in response:

  #3 (ignored ok) ‚ÄĒ already covered, no code. A bound-but-unused insert/delete
  ok already trips the unused_local lint; _ is the explicit, intentional discard
  (the Go _ = err model). So ignoring a real ok is surfaced; deliberately
  discarding it is opt-in.

  #4 (sized-param .length) ‚ÄĒ fixed on the func path. The array own-thread func
  tests use a.length again instead of magic numbers. (Proc/monomorph sized-array
  params still don't carry length ‚ÄĒ the two fill procs keep their exact
  char[32] literal; documented.)

  #1 (real guarantees) ‚ÄĒ local-buffer gating added. This was the substantive
  one. "Total" now covers indexing of explicitly-typed local arrays, not just
  params ‚ÄĒ closing the biggest hole. Fallout handled per your "use proc! where
  we can't verify ‚ÄĒ so be it":
  - The 4 *_array_oob tests now fail to compile (the guarantee catching the OOB
  statically) instead of aborting at runtime ‚ÄĒ converted to compile-error
  assertions.
  - router.add's local segbuf guarded so the stdlib router stays total.
  - The 5 csv test loaders marked proc! (safe-but-unprovable buffer scanning ‚ÄĒ
  exactly your "can't cheaply verify" case).

  One deliberate non-change I want to flag: I did not elide the runtime bounds
  checks. Eliding based on a hand-rolled prover would turn any prover bug into
  memory corruption; keeping them means a prover bug aborts loudly. So a total
  proc is guaranteed not to OOB-corrupt and is compile-checked free of
  unprovable indices in the gated categories ‚ÄĒ that's the strongest honest
  guarantee without a formally-trusted prover.

  Remaining boundary (your call): pool columns (Arch.field[i]), module statics,
  inferred-type locals, and slice-creation are still exempt. The big one is
  columns ‚ÄĒ gating them is impractical because column liveness is dynamic, so
  nearly all column code would become proc!. That's the one place a "total" proc
  can still abort (e.g. router's cap_start[cap_count[0]]). Say the word if you
  want columns gated too.

  All of this is updated in docs/TOTALITY_DECISIONS.md. Nothing committed yet.

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 14m 20s

‚ĚĮ what is left for concerns/decisions                                           

‚óŹ Here's the clean accounting ‚ÄĒ what's settled, what's genuinely still your
  call, and residual risk to just be aware of.

  Open decisions (your call)

  1. Pool-column gating ‚ÄĒ the one real remaining hole in the guarantee. Indexing
  Arch.field[i] (and module statics, slice-creation, inferred-type locals) is
  still exempt, so a "total" proc can still abort there at runtime ‚ÄĒ e.g.
  router's cap_start[cap_count[0]]. I left columns trusted because gating them
  is viral: column liveness is dynamic, so ~all column code would become proc!.
  Decision: leave columns trusted, or gate them and accept pervasive proc!?
  2. Trust the prover enough to elide runtime checks? Today "total" = "no
  unprovable index + runtime backstop," not "no abort path in the binary."
  Making it the latter (and getting the perf win) means trusting/auditing the
  prover for memory safety ‚ÄĒ a prover bug would then corrupt instead of abort.
  Decision: keep the safe backstop, or invest in a trusted prover + elision?
  3. Sized-array-param .length on the proc/monomorph paths. Fixed only on the
  func path; two fill procs still guard with the literal size (32). Fixing the
  proc ABI removes that inconsistency. Moderate effort, some ABI risk. Decision:
  fix now, or leave documented?
  4. Stricter ok handling? Right now ignoring insert/delete ok is caught by
  unused_local, and _ is an intentional discard (Go-style). Decision: leave 
  as-is, or add a dedicated lint that flags even _-discarded capacity failures?

  Residual risks (awareness, no decision needed)

  - Prover soundness is hand-verified, not proven ‚ÄĒ validated by "the 535-suite
  still passes," not by fuzzing/adversarial tests. Since checks aren't elided,
  an unsound case aborts loudly rather than corrupts ‚ÄĒ but it could wrongly
  reject (force a needless proc!) or wrongly accept (a latent abort the backstop
  catches).
  - delete is virally proc! (by your approval). Fine for occasional deletes;
  could feel heavy in code that deletes constantly (e.g. an ECS).
  - Two minor side-effects: the global &&/|| ‚Üí OP_AND/OP_OR mapping wasn't
  exhaustively audited against every sem_binary_op consumer (suite is green);
  and strcopy now truncates to min(src,dst) instead of assuming dst ‚Č• src.

  Settled

  A‚ÄďF all implemented; insert/delete mandatory-ok; contagion + E0095/E0096;
  local-buffer gating; analyzer ! hint; decisions logged in
  docs/TOTALITY_DECISIONS.md; clean build, everything green; nothing committed.

  Net: the only item that materially weakens the "a plain proc can't crash"
  promise is #1 (columns). Everything else is either a conscious tradeoff or low
  risk. Want me to take any of these?

‚óŹ All green after the lint + docs. Here's where #4 and #3 landed, plus the
  answers to #1 and #2:

  #4 ‚ÄĒ dedicated lint ‚úÖ done

  New W0016 discarded_ok: discarding insert/delete's ok with _ now warns ("a
  capacity/handle failure is silently ignored‚Ä¶ capture and check ok, or
  @allow(discarded_ok)"). It's distinct from unused_local (which only catches a
  bound-but-unused ok; _ was otherwise a silent intentional discard). Suite
  still 535/535 (lints are non-fatal and don't show in the test summary). The
  migrated sites that discard ok will surface it ‚ÄĒ intentionally.

  #3 ‚ÄĒ documented ‚úÖ

  Added to docs/TOTALITY_DECISIONS.md: the proc/monomorph sized-param .length
  inconsistency is left as-is pending your call on removing .length from arrays
  ‚ÄĒ since on a fixed T[N] it's redundant with N. If it goes, the func-path fix +
  array-test .length guards revert to literal sizes; if it stays, the proc ABI
  needs the same fix. I won't touch the proc ABI until that's settled.

  #1 ‚ÄĒ "do we even do this? just lint it?"

  You're right, and I was overcautious. Measured it: only ~28 dynamic 
  column-index sites in the whole tree, concentrated in the router trie
  (TrieNode.*[cur/child]), csv row-fills (Transaction.*[idx]), and ~4 example
  loops (Body.mass[i]). Constant column access (Particle.pos[0]) ‚ÄĒ the common
  case ‚ÄĒ is memory-safe against the static pool capacity (the column array is
  capacity long), so it'd never be flagged.

  So gating columns is not viral. A column has a static capacity (Arch[N]) and a
  dynamic count, with the invariant count ‚Č§ capacity. So it's provable when:
  index is a constant < capacity, or the loop is bounded by Arch.count/.length.
  Only the router's slot-traversal ([cur]/[child]) stays unprovable ‚Üí guard or
  proc!. Recommendation: add a discarded-style lint for any column/static index 
  the prover can't discharge (default-on warning, not a hard error) ‚ÄĒ that
  surfaces the whole guarantee gap everywhere (including the
  cap_start[cap_count[0]] bug) without forcing proc! churn, and you can promote
  it to an error later. Want me to implement that column/static-index lint?

  #2 ‚ÄĒ how other compilers handle this

  - Rust / Zig / Go: runtime bounds checks (panic/abort); the optimizer elides
  provably-redundant checks as a best-effort optimization, not a guarantee. No
  "total function" concept. (Zig drops checks in ReleaseFast; Rust offers
  get()‚ÜíOption.) This is essentially our runtime backstop without the
  proc!/totality classification.
  - C/C++: nothing.
  - Ada/SPARK: Ada has runtime checks; SPARK proves absence of run-time errors
  (incl. index-out-of-range) statically via SMT solvers (Z3/CVC5/Alt-Ergo
  through Why3), with programmer-supplied contracts/loop invariants. Gold
  standard, heavy.
  - WUFFS (Google): a language designed so all bounds are proven at compile
  time, no runtime checks in production ‚ÄĒ and crucially it uses a bounded 
  fact-checker, not an SMT solver, requiring the programmer to carry
  facts/assertions. This is almost exactly our approach (prove-or-reject with a
  pattern/fact checker) ‚ÄĒ except WUFFS elides the checks and trusts the checker.
  - Dependently typed / refinement (Idris/Agda/Lean/F*, Liquid Haskell): Vec 
  n+Fin n or SMT-refined predicates ‚ÄĒ OOB doesn't typecheck. True guarantee,
  highest cost.

  The takeaway for your elision decision (#2 from before): WUFFS is proof that a
  real no-runtime-check guarantee is achievable with a conservative non-SMT 
  fact-checker like ours ‚ÄĒ you just have to trust/audit the checker and keep the
  accepted patterns restricted (which we already do). So eliding isn't
  reckless; it's the WUFFS path. Mainstream languages (Rust/Zig) deliberately
  don't ‚ÄĒ they keep the runtime check and call it a day. So our current state
  (checker + backstop + proc! escape) sits between Rust and WUFFS, and moving to
  a true guarantee = "become WUFFS for the gated categories" (elide + trust)
  vs. "stay Rust-like" (keep backstop).

  Net remaining open decisions: (a) implement the column/static-index lint I
  recommended for #1; (b) the elide-vs-backstop call for a true guarantee (WUFFS
  vs Rust); (c) .length's fate. Want me to do (a) now?

‚ĚĮ yeah lets do a lint, say prefer handles or something.                         
                                                                                
  we will need to think through a panic recover system or something for oob

‚óŹ Good ‚ÄĒ two things: I'll answer the recover question (it's a key design point),
  then implement the lint.

  "If a proc recovers, it doesn't need to be proc!, right?"

  Exactly right ‚ÄĒ and that's the missing third option from your original design
  ("error at the place / handle it / guaranteed to work"). The model is:

  - proc! = propagates a panic (uncaught).
  - a recover boundary = handles it ‚Üí the panic doesn't escape ‚Üí the enclosing
  proc is total (no proc!).

  So contagion propagates can_panic up the call graph until it hits either a 
  proc! marker (propagate) or a recover block (absorb). A plain proc may call
  proc! code if it wraps it in recover. That's the clean dual, and it matches Go
  (defer recover() stops the panic), Swift (do/catch), etc.

  Your instinct to split by failure kind is the right one:
  - OOB / stale-handle (bugs): a recover boundary fits ‚ÄĒ e.g. a request handler
  that catches and returns 500 instead of dying. Needs the runtime unwind
  mechanism (signal/longjmp/unwinding).
  - Capacity (predictable resource): reservations that err cleanly at a boundary
  are better than recover ‚ÄĒ you plan it, so a single fallible reserve (or the
  ok value) beats catching a panic. (This is the ¬ßreservation idea from the very
  first conversation.)

  So: recover is the escape hatch for bug-class aborts; reservations/ok are for
  resource failures. A proc using either is total. Worth designing recover to
  only catch the bug-class aborts (OOB/stale), not silently swallow logic
  errors.

      101    "total" proc is guaranteed not to OOB-*corrupt*, and is comp

          -verything becomes `proc!`); flag if you

          +oc!` marker (propagate) or a recover

          +err cleanly** at a boundary (or the

          +ow logic errors.

      131    `a.length == b.length`); provable code that doesn't match a

      132    marked `proc!`. Soundness is hand-verified against the test

‚óŹ Done. Clean build, 535/535 + all unit + doctests + 599 roundtrip green.

  Lint shipped ‚ÄĒ W0017 raw_pool_index ("prefer handles"): warns when a pool
  column Arch.field[i] is indexed by an unproven raw slot ‚ÄĒ "prefer a 
  generation-checked handle (insert/delete), bound by Arch.length, or 
  @allow(raw_pool_index)." Verified it fires only on genuinely-raw slots (16
  advisory hits on the router's intrusive trie links) and not on constant or
  .length/.count-bounded column access. It's a once-per-site warning, never
  forces proc! ‚ÄĒ so it surfaces the whole guarantee gap (including the
  cap_start[cap_count[0]] case) without churn. Suite stays green (lints are
  non-fatal).

  Your recover question ‚ÄĒ yes, confirmed and it's the key piece:
  - A recover boundary absorbs the panic ‚áí the recovering proc is total (no
  proc!). Contagion propagates can_panic up until it hits either a proc! marker
  (propagate) or a recover block (handle). That's the clean dual and matches
  Go/Swift.
  - Split by failure kind, as you said: OOB / stale-handle (bugs) ‚Üí recover
  (needs a runtime unwind mechanism); capacity (predictable) ‚Üí reservations / ok
  that err cleanly, not recover. I noted this as the design direction in
  docs/TOTALITY_DECISIONS.md (under "Design direction: recover + reservations ‚ÄĒ
  not yet built").

  So the picture now:
  - Bugs (OOB/stale): runtime backstop today; future recover makes a handling
  proc total.
  - Capacity: errors-as-values (ok) today; future reservations for clean
  up-front planning.
  - Raw pool indexing: W0017 nudges toward handles.
  - Ignored ok: W0016 flags silent discards.

  Open for later (all documented): build the recover mechanism + reservation
  API; decide whether to gate columns (now shown feasible, ~28 sites) vs.
  lint-only; the elide-vs-backstop guarantee call (WUFFS vs Rust); and .length's
  fate. Nothing committed.

‚ĚĮ so no array oob checks that couldn't be elided?                               

‚óŹ Not quite ‚ÄĒ and the line between "elidable" and "not" is exactly the line
  between the gated and exempt categories. (Caveat: I never implemented elision
  ‚ÄĒ all checks are still emitted today. This is about what the prover currently
  establishes, i.e. what could be elided.)

  Elidable (proven in every total proc/func):
  - Array/slice parameters (s[i], buf[i])
  - Explicitly-typed local arrays (b: char[8]; b[i])

  For these, anything unprovable was forced to proc! or guarded, so by
  construction every such index in a plain proc is proven ‚Üí its check could be
  elided. None stuck.

  NOT elidable (the prover doesn't discharge these):
  - Pool columns (Arch.field[i]) ‚ÄĒ only linted (W0017), never proven. ~21 sites,
  16 of them the router trie. Of these:
    - constant index and i < Arch.length/.count loops are provable in principle
  (capacity is static, count ‚Č§ capacity) ‚ÄĒ I just don't prove them yet, so today
  their checks stay.
    - the router's ~16 raw-slot indices ([cur], [child]) are genuinely not 
  statically provable ‚ÄĒ dynamic slots from trie traversal. Those can never be
  elided without a guard, a handle redesign, or a recover. They'd remain real
  checks.
  - Module-static arrays (cap_start[cap_count[0]]) ‚ÄĒ not proven, not even
  linted.
  - Dynamic slice-creation (a[x:y]) ‚ÄĒ exempt.
  - Inferred-type locals (x := ‚Ä¶ then x[i], no explicit array type) ‚ÄĒ I made
  these exempt to avoid false positives, so they pass unproven and unsurfaced.
  This is the quiet gap: a value-array index that's neither proven nor flagged.

  So: for the gated value-array/local domain, yes ‚ÄĒ every OOB check is elidable.
  Outside it (columns, statics, dynamic slices, inferred locals), no. The
  irreducible core that could never be elided by any amount of this style of
  proving is the router's dynamic-slot column indexing (~16) ‚ÄĒ that genuinely
  needs a guard, a generation-checked handle, or a recover boundary, not a
  static proof.

  If you want me to close the "inferred-type local" gap (gate them like typed
  locals) or teach the prover the static-capacity/count‚Č§capacity facts so
  constant + count-bounded column access also become elidable, both are doable ‚ÄĒ
  that would shrink the non-elidable set down to just the genuinely-dynamic
  router slots.

‚úĽ Churned for 50s

‚ĚĮ we need to introduce a pattern. Maybe when you slice it implicitly uses min() 
  max() or something                                                            

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ this is the right primitive, and it's the "total by construction"
  sibling of the reservations idea (reservations make capacity clean; saturating
  slices make views clean). Let me work through it.

  Saturating slices: a[x:y] clamps instead of aborting

  Mechanism ‚ÄĒ exactly your min/max:
  lo = max(0, min(x, a.length))
  hi = max(lo, min(y, a.length))     // hi ‚Č• lo, both in [0, a.length]
  The result is always a valid view (possibly empty). So slice creation has no 
  abort path at all ‚ÄĒ and notably this replaces the bounds-check-and-abort with
  two branchless min/max, so it's total and about as cheap (often cheaper than a
  predicted branch + abort block). It's inherently elidable because there's
  nothing to elide.

  What it unlocks

  This is the missing provable pattern for the cases that currently can't be
  proven:

  - Derived indices (arr[start+i]) ‚ÄĒ the thing that forced hand-written guards
  in seg_eq/name_eq/find_char. With saturating slices you write w := 
  arr[start:end] (total) then iterate w[i] with i < w.length ‚ÄĒ which the
  existing prover already discharges. All those guards I added disappear, and
  the code reads better.
  - Sub-range column access ‚ÄĒ Particle.pos[a:b] becomes a total clamped view;
  iterate it provably. So range column access stops being a panic site.
  - The slice-creation gap (currently exempt from both gating and the lint)
  closes entirely.

  So the totality story becomes: express access as slices + iteration ‚Üí total by
  construction. That fits the data-oriented grain of the language and is
  genuinely the pattern to push.

  What it does not fix

  Single-element random access: a[i], and especially the router's col[cur]. A
  slice is a range primitive; clamping a single index has no sensible answer
  (you'd return the wrong element or a sentinel ‚ÄĒ worse than a slice's empty
  view). So random single-element indexing stays in the proof / guard / handle /
  recover regime. The router's ~16 raw-slot accesses aren't helped by this ‚ÄĒ
  they need handles or guards.

  The one real decision: clamp silently, or keep a loud form?

  Saturating trades a loud abort for a silently-short/empty view. For views
  that's defensible (you asked for [x:y], you get the valid intersection; check
  .length if the size matters) ‚ÄĒ Python slices work this way. But it can hide a
  logic bug. Two coherent options:

  1. Clamp by default, drop the aborting slice form ‚ÄĒ consistent with how we did
  mandatory-ok insert (the dangerous form is just gone). Simplest, fully total,
  one way to slice.
  2. Clamp is default; a strict/checked slice is the proc!/recover form ‚ÄĒ keeps
  an abort for invariant-checking when you want it.

  I'd recommend #1 unless you specifically want slice-OOB to be a detectable
  bug. Either way: single-index should not clamp (keep it proof-or-proc!), only
  ranges.

  Consequences if we build it

  - tests/.../arrays/slice_oob_rejected.arche inverts (slice no longer aborts) ‚ÄĒ
  convert like the *_array_oob tests.
  - The stdlib guards I hand-wrote (seg_eq, name_eq, find_char, strcopy, the
  fill procs) simplify to slice-then-iterate.
  - Codegen: emit_slice_bounds_check ‚Üí emit clamp (min/max) instead of
  check+abort.
  - Prover: slice-creation drops out of the "can panic" set; a saturated slice's
  .length is a known runtime bound (already handled).

  Want me to spec this out (and the recover/reservation siblings) as a plan, or
  prototype saturating slices directly? My inclination: prototype a[x:y]
  clamping first since it's self-contained, high-leverage, and lets me delete a
  bunch of the guard code I added ‚ÄĒ then we'd see the guard-free stdlib as proof
  it works.

‚úĽ Cogitated for 1m 31s

‚ĚĮ slice oob should still fail to compile for constants or easily provable cases 
  like ti                                                                       

‚óŹ Agreed ‚ÄĒ that's the right call, and it keeps slices honest: clamp the dynamic,
  reject the provable mistake. Silently clamping a[0:100] on a char[8] would
  hide an obvious bug. So:

  The rule

  For a[x:y]:
  - Both bounds and a's size statically known ‚Üí check at compile time; error on
  x>y, y>size, or x<0. (Catches a[2:100] on char[8], inverted a[5:2], etc.)
  - In-bounds and provable ‚Üí no check, no clamp ‚ÄĒ it's just valid.
  - Otherwise (dynamic bounds, or dynamic-size array) ‚Üí runtime clamp
  (saturating min/max), total.

  So: provable-OOB = compile error; provably-fine = free; only the
  genuinely-unprovable falls back to clamp. Same split we already use for
  indexing, just with "clamp" as the dynamic fallback instead of "force proc!."

  It reuses what's already there

  The prover already has exactly the inputs: bnd_lit_int (constant bounds),
  sized-array ranks + tracked local sizes, and the min-length facts. So "easily
  provable" extends naturally:
  - Constant y > N into a sized T[N] (or a slice with a proven minlen) ‚Üí error.
  - Constant x > y ‚Üí error.
  - a[lo:hi] with anything dynamic, or a a dynamic-size char[] param where the
  constant can't be disproven ‚Üí clamp.

  (Note the asymmetry by array kind: on a fixed T[N] we can prove a[0:100] wrong
  ‚Üí error; on a char[] param the length is runtime, so a constant end can't be
  statically disproven ‚Üí it clamps. That's correct ‚ÄĒ we only hard-error what we
  can actually prove wrong.)

  So the three regimes line up

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā   form    ‚Ēā   provably    ‚Ēā provably OOB ‚Ēā         unprovable          ‚Ēā

  ‚Ēā index     ‚Ēā ‚úÖ free       ‚Ēā ‚ĚĆ compile   ‚Ēā ‚ĚĆ compile error ‚Üí guard /  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā a[i]      ‚Ēā               ‚Ēā error        ‚Ēā proc! / recover             ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā slice     ‚Ēā ‚úÖ free       ‚Ēā ‚ĚĆ compile   ‚Ēā ‚§Ķ runtime clamp (total)     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā a[x:y]    ‚Ēā               ‚Ēā error        ‚Ēā                             ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  Indexing can't clamp (no sensible single-element fallback), so unprovable
  index = error. Slicing can clamp, so unprovable slice = total-by-clamp.
  Provable-OOB is a compile error for both ‚ÄĒ that's your point, and it's the
  consistent rule.

  This is a small, clean extension of the existing bounds analysis plus a

  min/max clamp). Want me to fold it into the saturating-slice prototype ‚ÄĒ i.e.,
  build: (1) constant/known-size slice bounds ‚Üí hard error, (2) everything else
  ‚Üí clamp, (3) convert slice_oob_rejected to a compile-error test, (4) delete
  the now-unnecessary stdlib guards?

‚úĽ Crunched for 49s

‚ĚĮ if we force every panicable operation to have a recover do we even need proc! 
  ?                                                                             

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ I've read the existing plan (it's the completed A‚ÄďF work). Your question is a
  forward-looking architecture decision, and I know this subsystem cold from
  building it, so let me reason it out directly rather than re-explore.

  The honest answer

  You always need the panic-tracking analysis (knowing which ops can abort and
  verifying each is dealt with). proc! is just one of two ways to discharge that
  effect:

  - proc! = propagate ("I don't handle it; it bubbles up ‚ÄĒ ultimately to main,
  where it crashes").
  - recover = handle ("caught here; nothing escapes above me").

  They're duals. So with recover, proc!'s only remaining job is to let a panic
  propagate uncaught. If you forbid that ‚ÄĒ force every panic-able op to be
  recovered ‚ÄĒ then nothing propagates and the proc! marker becomes unnecessary.
  The contagion analysis stays; it just changes from "is this marked proc!?" to
  "does this have a recover ancestor?" (compile error if not).

  But you can't have all three of: {no proc! marker, allow "let it crash",
  at-a-glance "can't crash" guarantee}. Pick the corner:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā      Design       ‚Ēā marker? ‚Ēā      fail-fast       ‚Ēā    guarantee?     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                   ‚Ēā         ‚Ēā   (let-it-crash)?    ‚Ēā                   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Keep proc! + add  ‚Ēā yes     ‚Ēā yes (marked)         ‚Ēā yes               ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā recover           ‚Ēā         ‚Ēā                      ‚Ēā                   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Drop proc!,       ‚Ēā no      ‚Ēā no (must recover     ‚Ēā yes               ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā mandate recover   ‚Ēā         ‚Ēā even bugs)           ‚Ēā                   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Drop proc!, allow ‚Ēā no      ‚Ēā yes                  ‚Ēā no ‚ÄĒ silent       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā  uncaught         ‚Ēā         ‚Ēā                      ‚Ēā crashes return    ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The third is a regression (it's where we started). So the real fork is the
  first two.

  Why this is even on the table now: we've made most things total by
  construction ‚ÄĒ proven indexing, soon clamped slices, ok-valued insert. So the
  residual panic-able set is tiny (~30 sites: delete, raw-column index,
  divide-by-zero, statics). When the things that can panic are that rare, "just
  recover them" stops being burdensome ‚ÄĒ which is exactly why dropping proc! is
  suddenly viable. The cost of dropping it is purely: for a bug like OOB/stale
  where you'd happily just crash in dev, you'd now have to write a recover
  (ceremony) instead of letting it propagate.

  A nuance worth noting: you could keep a single fail-fast escape by making main
  (or a designated entry) the one implicit "recover-or-abort" boundary ‚ÄĒ then
  bugs still crash at the top without per-site recover, but everywhere else must
  recover or be total. That recovers most of proc!'s ergonomics with no general
  marker.

  The decision is really about fail-fast vs. strictness, so:

‚óŹ¬†User declined to answer questions
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ With a `recover` mechanism, how should panic-capability be discharged ‚ÄĒ 
     keep `proc!` as the propagate-marker, or drop it and make `recover` the 
     sole discharge? (Drop proc!, recover-only / Keep proc! + add recover)
     ¬∑ Should there be a single implicit 'let it crash' boundary so a bug 
     (OOB/stale) can still abort without a hand-written recover at the site? 
     (main is implicit boundary / No implicit boundary)

‚ĚĮ is there a reason  to have a recover ancestor instead of it being in the same 
  proc always                                                                   

‚óŹ Great question ‚ÄĒ and it cuts deeper than the one I asked. Let me reason it
  out.

  What "recover must be in the same proc" actually buys you

  If a panic-able op must be recovered in its own proc (no ancestor), then no 
  proc ever propagates a panic ‚ÄĒ every proc handles its own internally, so every
  proc is total from its caller's view. And that cascades:

  - No contagion. There's no cross-call can_panic effect to track ‚Üí no
  call-graph fixpoint, no proc! marker. The check becomes purely local: "does
  this proc prove-or-recover every panic-able op it contains?" A per-proc pass,
  not a whole-program one. The entire subsystem I built collapses to a local
  check.
  - No unwinding runtime. A local recover is just a branch ‚ÄĒ a[i] else 
  <fallback> compiles to check-then-else, no stack unwinding. An ancestor
  recover needs real unwinding (signals/longjmp/DWARF), which in a no-heap
  language tangles with RAII, opaque-consumption, and cleanup. Same-proc recover
  sidesteps all of that.
  - Cross-proc failures become values, by force. If a helper can fail and the
  caller should decide, it can't propagate a panic ‚ÄĒ it must return ... (ok).
  That's exactly the errors-as-values direction you already chose for
  insert/delete. No hidden control flow.

  So the reasons to allow a recover ancestor are only the two things exceptions
  are good at:
  1. Deep bail-out ‚ÄĒ unwinding out of nested recursion without threading a value
  up each level (parser-style).
  2. Catch-all boundaries ‚ÄĒ "recover anything below this point" (a request
  handler that turns any failure into a¬†500).

  And arche has weak demand for both: it's iterative/data-oriented (the router
  is a loop, not deep recursion), and its whole ethos is no hidden control flow
  ‚ÄĒ which ancestor-propagation violates and value-returning honors.

  So: is there a reason? Essentially no, for arche.

  Same-proc-only recover is strictly simpler (no contagion, no proc!, no
  unwinding runtime) and pushes failures to be explicit values across
  boundaries. The only thing you give up is exception-style deep bail-out /
  catch-all ‚ÄĒ which fights the language's grain anyway. With that, a panic-able
  op has exactly three local discharges:

  - proven safe (no panic), or
  - recovered in-proc (expr else ‚Ä¶ ‚ÄĒ a branch), or
  - explicit assert/crash (you opted into aborting; marks the site, not the
  whole proc ‚ÄĒ strictly better than proc!'s per-proc marker).

  That last one even preserves fail-fast for genuine bugs, at the site, without
  any propagation marker. So proc! and the contagion pass would both go away.

  The one real fork left:

‚óŹ¬†User answered Claude's questions:
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ Should recover be same-proc-only (collapsing proc!/contagion and needing 
     no unwinding runtime), or allow ancestor propagation (exception-style)? ‚Üí 
     Same-proc only
  ‚éŅ ¬†Interrupted ¬∑ What should Claude do instead?

‚ĚĮ we need a clear system. I don't mind the defer recover thing like go but if   
  we aren't unwinding it might not be needed.                                   
                                                                                
  I like potentially resuing the policy system you could do something like

  ! could mean "policy for handling panic"                                      

‚óŹ That clicks the whole thing into place. Let me state the clear system, because
  I think your !policy idea unifies everything we've circled around.

  The system: failure policies (! = "how this op handles failure")

  One rule: an operation that can fail at runtime must be either statically 
  proven safe, or carry a failure policy. No proof + no policy = compile error.
  The policy makes the failure deterministic at the site ‚ÄĒ so it's resolved
  locally, no unwinding, no propagation.

  !policy generalizes proc! ‚ÄĒ ! everywhere means "failure-handling policy":

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā         op          ‚Ēā                     policies                      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā index / slice a[i], ‚Ēā !clamp (saturate), !zero (default / skip write),  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā  a[x:y]             ‚Ēā !wrap (modular), !abort (crash)                   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā insert(P,x)         ‚Ēā !reject (drop), !evict (ring), !abort, or (h:,    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                     ‚Ēā ok:) (report as value)                            ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā delete(h)           ‚Ēā !abort (stale crashes), or (ok:) (report)         ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā a / b               ‚Ēā !zero, !wrap, !abort                              ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  Total vs crashing policies: everything except !abort (and the report (ok:)
  form) is total ‚ÄĒ the op cannot crash. !abort is the only crashing policy, and
  it marks the exact site.

  This makes the original at-a-glance goal sharper than proc! did:
  - func may use only total policies ‚Üí a func never crashes, guaranteed
  (preserves "funcs are reliable").
  - proc may also !abort ‚Üí a proc crashes only at a visible !abort site ‚ÄĒ marked
  at the line, not smeared across the whole proc.

  Layering reuses the pool-policy idea from the start: a pool sets a default
  (Particle[100] !evict); a per-op !policy overrides it.

  What this replaces / reuses

  - Gone: proc!, the can_panic contagion pass, recover/unwinding (you nailed it
  ‚ÄĒ with no unwinding, Go's defer/recover isn't needed).
  - Reused: the bounds prover (it's now the "proven, so no policy needed" half),
  and the (ok:) form (it's just the report policy). The ~150 migrated insert
  sites stay valid.
  - Net: every fallible op is proven | total-policy | !abort ‚ÄĒ local, explicit,
  no whole-program effect tracking.

  A couple of decisions I want to lock before I write the plan:

‚óŹ¬†User answered Claude's questions:
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ Should the policy system fully replace `proc!` + the can_panic contagion 
     pass (rip them out), or keep `proc!` alongside policies? ‚Üí Replace proc! 
     with policies
     ¬∑ When a fallible op is neither proven safe nor given a policy, what 
     happens? ‚Üí everything will have a default policy, sensible defaults. Lsp 
     hints will be a must for implicit policies

‚óŹ Both locked: policies replace proc!/contagion entirely, and every fallible op 
  gets a sensible default policy (no annotation required) with LSP hints 
  surfacing the implicit policy (mandatory). I have complete context on every
  touch point from building the current system, so I'll write the plan directly
  rather than re-explore. Let me record it.

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ Plan recorded. The key shift: !policy per operation replaces proc! + contagion
  + recover entirely ‚ÄĒ failures resolve locally and deterministically (no
  unwinding), every fallible op has a sensible default policy with mandatory LSP
  hints, func stays crash-proof (total policies only), proc crashes only at
  explicit !abort sites, and slices default to !clamp (provably-OOB constants
  still error). The bounds prover and (ok:) form survive; proc!/E0095/contagion
  get ripped out.

  Two minor items are flagged in the plan for confirmation on review (func index
  default = !clamp; single-index clamp read/write semantics), and
  !evict/!wrap/divide-policies/check-elision are scoped to a later milestone.  ‚éŅ ¬†User rejected Claude's plan:
     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā Plan: failure policies (!policy) ‚ÄĒ replace proc!/contagion              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The proc! + whole-program can_panic contagion model (just built) is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā heavier than arche needs.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā After making most things total by construction (proven indexing,        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ok-valued insert, soon-clamped                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slices), the residual set of operations that can fail at runtime is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tiny (~30 sites). So instead of                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a propagation marker + call-graph effect analysis + (proposed)          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā recover/unwinding, we resolve each                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure locally, at the operation, by a policy ‚ÄĒ expr !policy. This     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā needs no unwinding, no                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā contagion, and gives a sharper guarantee than proc!: a func provably    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā never crashes; a proc                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crashes only at a visible !abort site (marked at the line, not smeared  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā over the whole proc).                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ! is unified to mean "failure-handling policy" (generalizing proc!),    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reusing the pool                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overload-policy idea from the original design discussion (Particle[100] ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict).                                                                ‚Ēā

‚óŹ Good thing to pin down ‚ÄĒ "lowest gen + lowest id" is clever but has a
  subtlety. Let me evaluate the options for which row !evict destroys when the
  pool is full:

  1. "lowest gen + lowest id" (your idea). Uses metadata we already have ‚ÄĒ no
  new fields. But gen is recycle count, not age: a long-lived row that was never
  deleted has a low gen, a churned slot has a high gen. So min-gen ‚Č† oldest.
  What it does do: each evict bumps the victim's gen, pushing it out of the
  min-gen set, so repeated evicts emergently walk slots in id order ‚Čą
  round-robin. Two problems: it costs an O(cap) scan per evict to find the min,
  and the semantics ("least-recycled, lowest index") are non-obvious. A cursor
  gets the same round-robin in O(1).

  2. Ring cursor (recommended). Pool keeps one head. On a full insert: victim = 
  head; head = (head+1) % cap. O(1), one i64 field, and it's the standard
  ring-buffer "overwrite the oldest in the ring" ‚ÄĒ exact FIFO for the streaming
  case !evict is meant for. Strictly dominates option 1 (same behavior, no
  scan).

  3. Born-sequence column (exact oldest, always). A per-row monotonic insert
  seq; evict the true minimum. Correct even under arbitrary delete/insert churn,
  but needs an i64 column and an O(cap) scan (or a min-heap for O(log cap)).
  Only worth it if you need real global-oldest under heavy mixed delete/insert.

  Safety invariant (all three): evicting must bump the victim's generation (with
  the same gen-exhaustion check as delete), so the evicted occupant's handle
  goes stale and any later use is caught. !evict silently destroys a row ‚ÄĒ so an
  !evict pool is for anonymous streamed collectives (particles, a log/audio
  ring), not rows you hold stable handles to. (That's the original convo-1
  conclusion: eviction pools shouldn't hand out long-lived handles.)

  So the mechanism for insert(P,x) !evict when full = victim = head; 
  head=(head+1)%cap; bump gen[victim]; overwrite columns[victim]; return (victim
  | gen<<32). Count stays at cap; the free-list is untouched (all slots live).

  My recommendation is the ring cursor ‚ÄĒ but the real question is whether you
  want exact age-ordering under churn:

‚óŹ¬†User answered Claude's questions:
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ How should `!evict` choose its victim when the pool is full? ‚Üí Ring 
     cursor (O(1))

‚óŹ Ring cursor it is. Let me update the plan with the resolved !evict mechanism.

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ !evict resolved: ring cursor ‚ÄĒ victim = head; head = (head+1) % cap; bump 
  gen[victim] (O(1), one i64 field, stales the evicted handle). Captured in the
  plan, with implementation deferred to a later milestone but the mechanism
  fixed.

  The plan is complete: the !policy system replacing proc!/contagion, per-op
  defaults + mandatory LSP hints, func crash-proof / proc !abort-at-site, slice
  !clamp default with provable-OOB-const errors, the bounds prover + (ok:)
  retained, ring-cursor !evict, and a v1/deferred scope split. Two minor items
  remain flagged for confirmation on review (func index default !clamp;
  single-index clamp read/write semantics).
