     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā Plan: failure policies (!policy) ‚ÄĒ replace proc!/contagion              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The proc! + whole-program can_panic contagion model (just built) is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā heavier than arche needs.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā After making most things total by construction (proven indexing,        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ok-valued insert, soon-clamped                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slices), the residual set of operations that can fail at runtime is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tiny (~30 sites). So instead of                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a propagation marker + call-graph effect analysis + (proposed)          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā recover/unwinding, we resolve each                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure locally, at the operation, by a policy ‚ÄĒ expr !policy. This     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā needs no unwinding, no                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā contagion, and gives a sharper guarantee than proc!: a func provably    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā never crashes; a proc                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crashes only at a visible !abort site (marked at the line, not smeared  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā over the whole proc).                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ! is unified to mean "failure-handling policy" (generalizing proc!),    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reusing the pool                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overload-policy idea from the original design discussion (Particle[100] ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict).                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Locked decisions                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Replace proc! and the can_panic contagion pass entirely. Keep the     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bounds prover                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (sem_bounds* in semantic.c) and the (h:, ok:) report form. No recover / ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā no stack unwinding.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Every fallible op has a sensible DEFAULT policy (unannotated code     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compiles); !policy                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides. LSP/analyzer hints surfacing the implicit policy are         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mandatory.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func = total policies only (can never crash). proc may also !abort.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Slices default to !clamp; a provably-out-of-bounds constant           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slice/index is a compile error                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (don't silently clamp a statically-wrong access).                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The model                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā expr !policy attaches a deterministic failure resolution at the site.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are total (op                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā cannot crash) except !abort (explicit, site-marked crash) and the (ok:) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report form.                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The guarantee is about the policy, not the default: !abort ‚ÄĒ whether    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it's the implicit                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default or explicitly written ‚ÄĒ is the only thing that can crash. Any   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā non-!abort policy                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (default or explicit) never crashes, in theory, ever. So defaulting a   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proc op to !abort is fine                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (unannotated code crashes on the failure, exactly like today; the LSP   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hint surfaces the implicit                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort). A func can't use !abort (funcs stay crash-proof), so its       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default is the relevant                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā total policy (!clamp for index/slice, !zero for divide) ‚ÄĒ still no      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compile error, just a                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā total default. Writing any explicit total policy (!clamp, !reject,      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report, ‚Ä¶) guarantees no                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crash.                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Core guarantee: an op using anything other than !abort (a total policy, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā or the report (ok:)                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā form) can never abort at runtime ‚ÄĒ period. This includes                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā delete(h)(ok:): a stale handle                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā there returns ok=0 (total), it does not abort. Only !abort (delete's    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default) aborts on a stale                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā handle. (This refines the earlier "stale always aborts" decision: stale ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā aborts only under !abort.)                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Proven safe (bounds prover) ‚áí raw access, no policy code at all.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func + !abort (explicit or as the would-be default) ‚áí compile error:  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a func must prove it or                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pick a total policy. (This is the one place a func "default" differs ‚ÄĒ  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proposed func index default                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !clamp; confirm on review.)                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pool layering: a pool decl sets the default (Particle[100] !evict); a ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā per-op !policy                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides it.                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are user-definable (built-ins are just shorthand)              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A policy is an ordinary func invoked on the failure path, with a        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā signature fixed by the op                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā category; the built-ins (clamp, wrap, evict, reject) are predefined     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy funcs in core/                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā stdlib. !name resolves to a policy func; a[i] !my_remap and insert(P,x) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !my_evictor work the                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā same as the built-ins.                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Index/slice policy: func(len: int, i: int) -> int ‚Üí the index to use. ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The language clamps                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the returned index into [0, len) as a final net, so no policy (even a   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā buggy user one) can                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā cause an OOB ‚ÄĒ that's what makes "never abort unless !abort" hold for   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā arbitrary policies.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Built-ins: clamp = identity-under-net, wrap = ((i%len)+len)%len.        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pool-full policy: func(<pool ctx>) -> int ‚Üí the victim slot to        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overwrite, or -1 to reject.                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Built-ins: evict (ring: return+advance head), reject (-1). User         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policies = custom victim                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā selectors (oldest, lowest-priority, random) ‚ÄĒ this is how !evict_oldest ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā becomes a library                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy, not a compiler built-in.                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Structural built-ins (not funcs): !abort (opts OUT of the net ‚Üí       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā abort) and the report                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (h:, ok:) form (routes the failure to an out-param). These can't be     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā user funcs.                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Constraints: a policy func must itself be total (no !abort inside) ‚ÄĒ  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā composes with the                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā func-total rule; the final-clamp net covers correctness. A policy may   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā declare per-pool metadata                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it needs (e.g. !evict_oldest's born-seq column), compiled into the pool ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā struct only for pools                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā that use it (pay-per-policy principle).                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - v1 ships the built-ins over this mechanism; the general user-policy   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā registration (resolving                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !name to a func, the per-category signature check, metadata             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā declaration) is the framework they                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compile to ‚ÄĒ phase the public "define your own policy" surface after    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the built-ins land.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - zero (return the element's zero / skip write) doesn't fit the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā index-remap shape ‚Üí keep it a                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā structural built-in, or drop it (open).                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Proposed policy syntax                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A policy form in the unified name :: <form> grammar, referenced !name;  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā signature shape picks                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the category; body must be total; built-ins are policy decls in core.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp :: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int {            // index/slice:   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā return index, net-clamped to [0,len)                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   if (i < 0) { return 0; }  if (i >= len) { return len - 1; }  return   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā i;                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā }                                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wrap  :: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int { return ((i % len) + len) %   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā len; }                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā v := samples[k] !wrap;   grid[x] !clamp = c;                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reject :: policy(cap: int) -> int { return 0 - 1; }   // pool-full:     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā victim slot, or -1 = reject                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā evict  :: policy(cap: int) -> int  uses { head: i64 } { v := head; head ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā = (head+1) % cap; return v; }                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Particle[1000] !evict;   insert(Particle, p);   insert(Particle, p)     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort;                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā zero :: policy(a: int, b: int) -> int { return 0; }   //                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā divide-by-zero: result when b==0                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā r := n / d !zero;                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - uses { ‚Ä¶ } = per-pool metadata, compiled in only for pools using the  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy (pay-per-policy).                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Empty-array edge (len==0, no valid index): the final net resolves     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā read‚Üízero / write‚Üískip ‚ÄĒ no abort.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Stateful pool policies (e.g. evict_oldest) need an on_insert(slot)    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hook and a                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā select_victim(cap)->slot|-1 hook ‚ÄĒ so the pool-policy interface is two  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hooks; the ring evict                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses only the victim hook. Spec the two-hook interface in the framework ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā milestone.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Structural (not policies): !abort (opt out of the net ‚Üí crash) and    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the report (h:,ok:) form.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā At each op, emit by resolved policy (replacing today's unconditional    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā check+abort):                                                           ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā clamp (slice) or clamped index; !zero ‚Üí in-bounds ? load : zero (skip   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā on write); !wrap ‚Üí                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā i % len.                                                                ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā !evict pool is for                                                      ‚Ēā

‚óŹ Right ‚ÄĒ that's a real contradiction on my part. If they live in core, they're
  standard-library policies written in arche, not built-ins. That's actually the
  strongest version of the idea: clamp/wrap/evict/reject have no special 
  compiler status ‚ÄĒ they're ordinary policy decls in core, identical to anything
  you'd write. The mechanism is fully general; core just ships the common ones
  (dogfooding).

  The genuinely compiler-intrinsic set is small ‚ÄĒ only the things that can't be
  expressed as a policy func:
  - !abort ‚ÄĒ aborts / opts out of the net (doesn't return an index).
  - report (h:, ok:) ‚ÄĒ routes failure to an out-param (a call-shape, not a
  func).
  - the final-clamp net ‚ÄĒ the compiler-applied safety that bounds any policy's
  result.
  - !zero ‚ÄĒ value-returning (-> elem), which doesn't fit the index-remap
  (len,i)->int shape and is ambiguous with it, so either it's intrinsic or needs
  an explicit category to be user-definable.

  Let me fix the terminology in the plan.

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

  consistency.

      "built-in\|builtin\|shorthand"

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ Fixed throughout. The plan now states it cleanly: clamp/wrap/evict/reject are
  ordinary core policies with no special compiler status (core dogfoods the
  mechanism), and the only true intrinsics ‚ÄĒ the parts that can't be a policy
  decl ‚ÄĒ are !abort, the report (ok:) form, the final-clamp net, and !zero
  (value-returning, so ambiguous with the index-remap shape).

  The full design is captured: !policy replaces proc!/contagion; policies are
  user-definable policy decls (!name); only !abort can ever crash (the net
  guarantees all other policies are crash-proof); core ships the common policies
  as plain library code; ring-cursor evict now + evict_oldest as a future
  library policy with pay-per-policy uses { ‚Ä¶ } metadata; the
  no-unexpected-abort guarantee tests; and the open items (fate of zero,
  single-index clamp semantics, exact policy signatures + two-hook pool
  interface).
  ‚éŅ ¬†User rejected Claude's plan:
     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā Plan: failure policies (!policy) ‚ÄĒ replace proc!/contagion              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The proc! + whole-program can_panic contagion model (just built) is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā heavier than arche needs.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā After making most things total by construction (proven indexing,        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ok-valued insert, soon-clamped                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slices), the residual set of operations that can fail at runtime is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tiny (~30 sites). So instead of                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a propagation marker + call-graph effect analysis + (proposed)          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā recover/unwinding, we resolve each                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure locally, at the operation, by a policy ‚ÄĒ expr !policy. This     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā needs no unwinding, no                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā contagion, and gives a sharper guarantee than proc!: a func provably    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā never crashes; a proc                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crashes only at a visible !abort site (marked at the line, not smeared  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā over the whole proc).                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ! is unified to mean "failure-handling policy" (generalizing proc!),    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reusing the pool                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overload-policy idea from the original design discussion (Particle[100] ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict).                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Locked decisions                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Replace proc! and the can_panic contagion pass entirely. Keep the     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bounds prover                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (sem_bounds* in semantic.c) and the (h:, ok:) report form. No recover / ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā no stack unwinding.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Every fallible op has a sensible DEFAULT policy (unannotated code     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compiles); !policy                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides. LSP/analyzer hints surfacing the implicit policy are         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mandatory.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func = total policies only (can never crash). proc may also !abort.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Slices default to !clamp; a provably-out-of-bounds constant           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slice/index is a compile error                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (don't silently clamp a statically-wrong access).                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The model                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā expr !policy attaches a deterministic failure resolution at the site.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are total (op                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā cannot crash) except !abort (explicit, site-marked crash) and the (ok:) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report form.                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā     op      ‚Ēā           policies           ‚Ēā   default (proc / func)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā !clamp, !wrap, !zero,        ‚Ēā !abort / !clamp          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā index a[i]  ‚Ēā !abort, user policy          ‚Ēā (provable-OOB const ‚áí    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                              ‚Ēā error)                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā slice       ‚Ēā                              ‚Ēā !abort / !clamp          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā a[x:y]      ‚Ēā !clamp, !abort, user policy  ‚Ēā (provable-OOB const ‚áí    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                              ‚Ēā error)                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā !reject, !evict, !abort,     ‚Ēā pool's declared policy,  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā insert(P,x) ‚Ēā (h:, ok:) report, user       ‚Ēā else !abort              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā policy                       ‚Ēā                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā delete(h)   ‚Ēā !abort, (ok:) report         ‚Ēā !abort                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā a / b       ‚Ēā !zero, !wrap, !abort         ‚Ēā !abort / !zero           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The guarantee is about the policy, not the default: !abort ‚ÄĒ whether    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it's the implicit                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default or explicitly written ‚ÄĒ is the only thing that can crash. Any   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā non-!abort policy                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (default or explicit) never crashes, in theory, ever. So defaulting a   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proc op to !abort is fine                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (unannotated code crashes on the failure, exactly like today; the LSP   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hint surfaces the implicit                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort). A func can't use !abort (funcs stay crash-proof), so its       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default is the relevant                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā total policy (!clamp for index/slice, !zero for divide) ‚ÄĒ still no      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compile error, just a                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā total default. Writing any explicit total policy (!clamp, !reject,      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report, ‚Ä¶) guarantees no                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crash.                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Core guarantee: an op using anything other than !abort (a total policy, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā or the report (ok:)                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā form) can never abort at runtime ‚ÄĒ period. This includes                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā delete(h)(ok:): a stale handle                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā there returns ok=0 (total), it does not abort. Only !abort (delete's    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default) aborts on a stale                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā handle. (This refines the earlier "stale always aborts" decision: stale ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā aborts only under !abort.)                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Proven safe (bounds prover) ‚áí raw access, no policy code at all.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func + !abort (explicit or as the would-be default) ‚áí compile error:  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a func must prove it or                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pick a total policy. (This is the one place a func "default" differs ‚ÄĒ  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proposed func index default                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !clamp; confirm on review.)                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pool layering: a pool decl sets the default (Particle[100] !evict); a ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā per-op !policy                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides it.                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are user-definable; core ships the common ones (they are NOT   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā built-ins)                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A policy is an ordinary policy decl invoked on the failure path (in the ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unified name :: <form>                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā grammar), with a signature fixed by the op category.                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp/wrap/evict/reject are just policy                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā decls in core, with no special compiler status ‚ÄĒ identical to anything  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a user writes. !name                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā resolves to a policy decl wherever it's visible (core or user). This is ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the whole point: the                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mechanism is fully general and core dogfoods it.                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Index/slice policy: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int ‚Üí the index to    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā use. The compiler clamps                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the returned index into [0, len) as a final net (and resolves len==0 to ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā read‚Üízero / write‚Üí                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā skip), so no policy (even a buggy user one) can cause an OOB ‚ÄĒ that's   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā what makes "never abort                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unless !abort" hold for arbitrary policies. core: clamp, wrap.          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pool-full policy: two hooks ‚ÄĒ optional on_insert(slot) (bookkeeping)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā select_victim(cap) -> slot | -1 (victim, or -1 = reject). core: evict   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (ring; victim hook +                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses { head }), reject. User policies = custom selectors (evict_oldest, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā lowest-priority,                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā random); evict_oldest is therefore a library policy, not anything       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā special.                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Compiler intrinsics (the only non-policy parts ‚ÄĒ can't be written as  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a policy): !abort                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (aborts / opts out of the net), the report (h:, ok:) form (routes       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure to an out-param), the                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā final-clamp net, and !zero (value-returning -> elem, which is ambiguous ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā with the index-remap                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā shape ‚Üí intrinsic, unless we add an explicit policy category to make it ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā user-definable ‚ÄĒ open).                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Constraints: a policy must itself be total (no !abort inside) ‚ÄĒ       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā composes with func-total;                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the net covers correctness. A policy may declare per-pool metadata via  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses { ‚Ä¶ }, compiled                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā into the pool struct only for pools that use it (pay-per-policy).       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Phasing: v1 can hardcode clamp/wrap/evict/reject while the general    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy decl +                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !name resolution + signature/category checking + uses metadata land;    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the end state is that                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā those four are just core policies with no compiler special-casing.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - zero (return the element's zero / skip write) doesn't fit the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā index-remap shape ‚Üí keep it a                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā structural built-in, or drop it (open).                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Proposed policy syntax                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A policy form in the unified name :: <form> grammar, referenced !name;  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā signature shape picks                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the category; body must be total; clamp/wrap/evict/reject are ordinary  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy decls in                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā core (no special status), shown here as examples.                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp :: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int {            // index/slice:   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā return index, net-clamped to [0,len)                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   if (i < 0) { return 0; }  if (i >= len) { return len - 1; }  return   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā i;                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā }                                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wrap  :: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int { return ((i % len) + len) %   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā len; }                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā v := samples[k] !wrap;   grid[x] !clamp = c;                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reject :: policy(cap: int) -> int { return 0 - 1; }   // pool-full:     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā victim slot, or -1 = reject                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā evict  :: policy(cap: int) -> int  uses { head: i64 } { v := head; head ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā = (head+1) % cap; return v; }                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Particle[1000] !evict;   insert(Particle, p);   insert(Particle, p)     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort;                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā zero :: policy(a: int, b: int) -> int { return 0; }   //                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā divide-by-zero: result when b==0                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā r := n / d !zero;                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - uses { ‚Ä¶ } = per-pool metadata, compiled in only for pools using the  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy (pay-per-policy).                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Empty-array edge (len==0, no valid index): the final net resolves     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā read‚Üízero / write‚Üískip ‚ÄĒ no abort.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Stateful pool policies (e.g. evict_oldest) need an on_insert(slot)    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hook and a                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā select_victim(cap)->slot|-1 hook ‚ÄĒ so the pool-policy interface is two  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hooks; the ring evict                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses only the victim hook. Spec the two-hook interface in the framework ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā milestone.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Structural (not policies): !abort (opt out of the net ‚Üí crash) and    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the report (h:,ok:) form.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Phases                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P1 ‚ÄĒ Parser: expr !policy                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Postfix !ident on index / slice / call expressions. ! already lexes as  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā TOK_BANG (Phase A). The                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy ident becomes a leaf/child on the op node. Touch:                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā parser/parser.c (postfix-expr parsing for                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā SN_INDEX_EXPR / SN_SLICE_EXPR / SN_CALL/PROC_CALL). Remove the proc!    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā marker parse (Phase-A                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā parse_proc_marker-style !-after-proc), since proc! is gone.             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P2 ‚ÄĒ Remove proc! / contagion                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Delete: the can_panic/can_panic_marked fields (hir.h, sem_decls.h),     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sem_check_panic_contagion                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and the panic_walk/decl_body_panicky_callee helpers, E0095              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā panic_in_total, and the                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā analyzer proc! hint. Keep sem_bounds* (the prover) and bnd_* fact       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā machinery ‚ÄĒ repurposed:                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā "proven ‚áí no policy; unprovable ‚áí apply policy."                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P3 ‚ÄĒ Policy resolution (semantic)                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā For each fallible op: resolve policy = explicit !policy else            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default(op-kind, pool-policy). Validate                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā func-total (no !abort in a func). Provable-OOB constant ‚áí error (reuse  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bnd_lit_int + sized/min-len                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā facts). Attach the resolved policy to the op via a cst_id-keyed side    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā table (like the existing                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sem_model side-model) so codegen reads it. Repurpose E0096 / add policy ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā diagnostics as needed.                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P4 ‚ÄĒ Codegen per policy                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā At each op, emit by resolved policy (replacing today's unconditional    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā check+abort):                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - index/slice !abort ‚Üí current                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā emit_bounds_check/emit_slice_bounds_check; !clamp ‚Üí min/max             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp (slice) or clamped index; !zero ‚Üí in-bounds ? load : zero (skip   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā on write); !wrap ‚Üí                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā i % len.                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - insert ‚Üí !abort (current overflow-abort), !reject (no-op + sentinel), ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report (h:,ok:)                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (current mandatory-ok helper). !evict = ring cursor: pool gains one i64 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā head; on a full                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā insert do victim = head; head = (head+1) % cap; bump gen[victim] (same  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā gen-exhaustion check as                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā delete ‚ÄĒ this stales the evicted occupant's handle), overwrite          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā columns[victim], return                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (victim | gen<<32); count stays at cap, free-list untouched. O(1). ‚áí an ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict pool is for                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā anonymous streamed collectives, not rows you hold stable handles to.    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Implementation deferred                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā to a later milestone (adds the head field to the pool struct + the      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā full-path branch in the                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā insert helper), but the mechanism is fixed.                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - delete ‚Üí !abort (current stale-abort), report (ok:).                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - divide policies ‚ÄĒ defer (!abort only in v1, = current behavior).      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Touch: codegen/codegen.c (emit_bounds_check 4485,                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā emit_slice_bounds_check 1855, insert helper                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 6859/overflow, delete helper 7026; index/slice/insert/delete call       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā lowering). Optional: elide policy                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā code when the prover proved the op safe (perf; deferrable ‚ÄĒ the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā guarantee comes from func-total, not                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā from elision).                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P5 ‚ÄĒ LSP hints (mandatory)                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Analyzer emits the implicit/explicit policy as an inlay at each         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā fallible op site. Reuse the                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā emit_effect_hint/emit_panic_hint infra in arche_analyzer.c ‚ÄĒ render     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā e.g. ghost !abort /                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !clamp after the op.                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā - The defensive guards added in stdlib (str/csv/router/io) can be       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā simplified to proofs or policies                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā over time; not required for green.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Scope / open items                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - v1 policies: !abort, !clamp, !zero (index/slice);                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort/!reject/report (insert);                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort/report (delete). Defer (mechanisms fixed): !evict (ring cursor ‚ÄĒ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā adds head to the                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pool struct), !wrap, divide policies, check elision.                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pay-per-policy metadata principle: policy-specific per-pool metadata  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is added to the pool                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā struct only when that pool actually uses the policy ‚ÄĒ !evict adds the   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā head cursor only to                                                     ‚Ēā

‚óŹ That's the enforcement layer that makes the guarantee usable ‚ÄĒ and it's the
  clean inverse of the old proc!: instead of marking code that may crash, you
  assert code that can't. Since !abort is the sole crash source, this is
  straightforward. Let me add it.

‚óŹ Let me add flag tests to the verification section, then re-present.

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ Added. The plan now has crash-free enforcement:
  - --no-abort ‚ÄĒ rejects any !abort (implicit or explicit) ‚Üí a provably
  crash-free binary (safety-critical builds).
  - --no-implicit-abort ‚ÄĒ rejects only the default !abort, forcing every
  fallible op to be explicitly annotated (-Werror-style "you didn't realize this
  could crash") while still allowing deliberate !abort.
  - Optional @total proc / #total { ‚Ä¶ } region ‚ÄĒ the precise inverse of proc!,
  scoping the guarantee to a critical section.

  Implementation is cheap: the policy-resolution pass already knows each op's
  resolved policy and whether it was explicit, so the flags just promote
  [implicit-]abort to an error in scope. Both flags get tests.

  That rounds out the full picture: !policy replaces proc!/contagion;
  user-definable policy decls with core shipping the common ones (no special
  status); !abort the sole crash source; the final-clamp net making every other
  policy crash-proof; ring evict + future evict_oldest (pay-per-policy uses
  metadata); the no-unexpected-abort guarantee tests; and now flags/attribute to
  assert crash-freedom.

     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā Plan: failure policies (!policy) ‚ÄĒ replace proc!/contagion              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The proc! + whole-program can_panic contagion model (just built) is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā heavier than arche needs.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā After making most things total by construction (proven indexing,        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ok-valued insert, soon-clamped                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slices), the residual set of operations that can fail at runtime is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tiny (~30 sites). So instead of                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a propagation marker + call-graph effect analysis + (proposed)          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā recover/unwinding, we resolve each                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure locally, at the operation, by a policy ‚ÄĒ expr !policy. This     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā needs no unwinding, no                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā contagion, and gives a sharper guarantee than proc!: a func provably    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā never crashes; a proc                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crashes only at a visible !abort site (marked at the line, not smeared  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā over the whole proc).                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ! is unified to mean "failure-handling policy" (generalizing proc!),    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reusing the pool                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overload-policy idea from the original design discussion (Particle[100] ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict).                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Locked decisions                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Replace proc! and the can_panic contagion pass entirely. Keep the     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bounds prover                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (sem_bounds* in semantic.c) and the (h:, ok:) report form. No recover / ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā no stack unwinding.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Every fallible op has a sensible DEFAULT policy (unannotated code     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compiles); !policy                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides. LSP/analyzer hints surfacing the implicit policy are         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mandatory.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func = total policies only (can never crash). proc may also !abort.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Slices default to !clamp; a provably-out-of-bounds constant           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slice/index is a compile error                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (don't silently clamp a statically-wrong access).                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The model                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā expr !policy attaches a deterministic failure resolution at the site.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are total (op                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā cannot crash) except !abort (explicit, site-marked crash) and the (ok:) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report form.                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā slice       ‚Ēā                              ‚Ēā !abort / !clamp          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā a[x:y]      ‚Ēā !clamp, !abort, user policy  ‚Ēā (provable-OOB const ‚áí    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                              ‚Ēā error)                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā !reject, !evict, !abort,     ‚Ēā pool's declared policy,  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā insert(P,x) ‚Ēā (h:, ok:) report, user       ‚Ēā else !abort              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā policy                       ‚Ēā                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā delete(h)   ‚Ēā !abort, (ok:) report         ‚Ēā !abort                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚Ēā a / b       ‚Ēā !zero, !wrap, !abort         ‚Ēā !abort / !zero           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The guarantee is about the policy, not the default: !abort ‚ÄĒ whether    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it's the implicit                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default or explicitly written ‚ÄĒ is the only thing that can crash. Any   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā non-!abort policy                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (default or explicit) never crashes, in theory, ever. So defaulting a   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proc op to !abort is fine                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (unannotated code crashes on the failure, exactly like today; the LSP   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hint surfaces the implicit                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort). A func can't use !abort (funcs stay crash-proof), so its       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default is the relevant                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā total policy (!clamp for index/slice, !zero for divide) ‚ÄĒ still no      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compile error, just a                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā total default. Writing any explicit total policy (!clamp, !reject,      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report, ‚Ä¶) guarantees no                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crash.                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Core guarantee: an op using anything other than !abort (a total policy, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā or the report (ok:)                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā form) can never abort at runtime ‚ÄĒ period. This includes                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā delete(h)(ok:): a stale handle                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā there returns ok=0 (total), it does not abort. Only !abort (delete's    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default) aborts on a stale                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā handle. (This refines the earlier "stale always aborts" decision: stale ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā aborts only under !abort.)                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Proven safe (bounds prover) ‚áí raw access, no policy code at all.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func + !abort (explicit or as the would-be default) ‚áí compile error:  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a func must prove it or                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pick a total policy. (This is the one place a func "default" differs ‚ÄĒ  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proposed func index default                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !clamp; confirm on review.)                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pool layering: a pool decl sets the default (Particle[100] !evict); a ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā per-op !policy                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides it.                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are user-definable; core ships the common ones (they are NOT   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā built-ins)                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A policy is an ordinary policy decl invoked on the failure path (in the ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unified name :: <form>                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā grammar), with a signature fixed by the op category.                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp/wrap/evict/reject are just policy                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā decls in core, with no special compiler status ‚ÄĒ identical to anything  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a user writes. !name                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā resolves to a policy decl wherever it's visible (core or user). This is ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the whole point: the                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mechanism is fully general and core dogfoods it.                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Index/slice policy: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int ‚Üí the index to    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā use. The compiler clamps                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the returned index into [0, len) as a final net (and resolves len==0 to ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā read‚Üízero / write‚Üí                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā skip), so no policy (even a buggy user one) can cause an OOB ‚ÄĒ that's   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā what makes "never abort                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unless !abort" hold for arbitrary policies. core: clamp, wrap.          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Pool-full policy: two hooks ‚ÄĒ optional on_insert(slot) (bookkeeping)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā select_victim(cap) -> slot | -1 (victim, or -1 = reject). core: evict   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (ring; victim hook +                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses { head }), reject. User policies = custom selectors (evict_oldest, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā lowest-priority,                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā random); evict_oldest is therefore a library policy, not anything       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā special.                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Compiler intrinsics (the only non-policy parts ‚ÄĒ can't be written as  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a policy): !abort                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (aborts / opts out of the net), the report (h:, ok:) form (routes       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure to an out-param), the                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā final-clamp net, and !zero (value-returning -> elem, which is ambiguous ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā with the index-remap                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā shape ‚Üí intrinsic, unless we add an explicit policy category to make it ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā user-definable ‚ÄĒ open).                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Constraints: a policy must itself be total (no !abort inside) ‚ÄĒ       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā composes with func-total;                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the net covers correctness. A policy may declare per-pool metadata via  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses { ‚Ä¶ }, compiled                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā into the pool struct only for pools that use it (pay-per-policy).       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Phasing: v1 can hardcode clamp/wrap/evict/reject while the general    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy decl +                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !name resolution + signature/category checking + uses metadata land;    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the end state is that                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā those four are just core policies with no compiler special-casing.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Crash-free enforcement (flags / attribute)                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Because !abort is the only crash source, crash-freedom is assertable ‚ÄĒ  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā this is the clean                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā inverse of the old proc! (assert it can't crash, instead of marking     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā that it may):                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - --no-abort (whole binary): any op resolving to !abort ‚ÄĒ implicit or   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā explicit ‚ÄĒ is a                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compile error ‚áí the binary provably cannot abort from a policy site.    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā For safety-critical builds.                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - --no-implicit-abort: only the implicit/default !abort errors ‚áí every  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā fallible op must be                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā explicitly annotated (!abort or a total policy). Closes the "didn't     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā realize this could crash"                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā gap (-Werror-style) while still allowing a deliberate, visible !abort.  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - (Option) per-proc / region attribute ‚ÄĒ e.g. a @total proc or a #total ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā { ‚Ä¶ } region that                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā scopes the no-abort guarantee to a critical section while the rest of   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the program may !abort.                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā This is the precise inverse of proc!.                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Implementation: the policy-resolution pass (P3) already knows each op's ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā resolved policy and whether                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it was explicit, so the flags/attribute just promote [implicit-]abort   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā to an error within scope ‚ÄĒ                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reusing the diagnostic infra. LSP still surfaces every implicit policy  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā regardless of the flags.                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - zero (return the element's zero / skip write) doesn't fit the         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā index-remap shape ‚Üí keep it a                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā structural built-in, or drop it (open).                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Proposed policy syntax                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A policy form in the unified name :: <form> grammar, referenced !name;  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā signature shape picks                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the category; body must be total; clamp/wrap/evict/reject are ordinary  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy decls in                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā core (no special status), shown here as examples.                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp :: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int {            // index/slice:   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā return index, net-clamped to [0,len)                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   if (i < 0) { return 0; }  if (i >= len) { return len - 1; }  return   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā i;                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā }                                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wrap  :: policy(len: int, i: int) -> int { return ((i % len) + len) %   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā len; }                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā v := samples[k] !wrap;   grid[x] !clamp = c;                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reject :: policy(cap: int) -> int { return 0 - 1; }   // pool-full:     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā victim slot, or -1 = reject                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā evict  :: policy(cap: int) -> int  uses { head: i64 } { v := head; head ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā = (head+1) % cap; return v; }                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Particle[1000] !evict;   insert(Particle, p);   insert(Particle, p)     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !abort;                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā zero :: policy(a: int, b: int) -> int { return 0; }   //                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā divide-by-zero: result when b==0                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā r := n / d !zero;                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - uses { ‚Ä¶ } = per-pool metadata, compiled in only for pools using the  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy (pay-per-policy).                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Empty-array edge (len==0, no valid index): the final net resolves     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā read‚Üízero / write‚Üískip ‚ÄĒ no abort.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Stateful pool policies (e.g. evict_oldest) need an on_insert(slot)    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hook and a                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā select_victim(cap)->slot|-1 hook ‚ÄĒ so the pool-policy interface is two  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā hooks; the ring evict                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā uses only the victim hook. Spec the two-hook interface in the framework ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā milestone.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Structural (not policies): !abort (opt out of the net ‚Üí crash) and    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the report (h:,ok:) form.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Phases                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P1 ‚ÄĒ Parser: expr !policy                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Postfix !ident on index / slice / call expressions. ! already lexes as  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā TOK_BANG (Phase A). The                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā policy ident becomes a leaf/child on the op node. Touch:                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā parser/parser.c (postfix-expr parsing for                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā SN_INDEX_EXPR / SN_SLICE_EXPR / SN_CALL/PROC_CALL). Remove the proc!    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā marker parse (Phase-A                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā parse_proc_marker-style !-after-proc), since proc! is gone.             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P2 ‚ÄĒ Remove proc! / contagion                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Delete: the can_panic/can_panic_marked fields (hir.h, sem_decls.h),     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sem_check_panic_contagion                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā and the panic_walk/decl_body_panicky_callee helpers, E0095              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā panic_in_total, and the                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā analyzer proc! hint. Keep sem_bounds* (the prover) and bnd_* fact       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā machinery ‚ÄĒ repurposed:                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā "proven ‚áí no policy; unprovable ‚áí apply policy."                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P3 ‚ÄĒ Policy resolution (semantic)                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā For each fallible op: resolve policy = explicit !policy else            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā default(op-kind, pool-policy). Validate                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā func-total (no !abort in a func). Provable-OOB constant ‚áí error (reuse  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bnd_lit_int + sized/min-len                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā facts). Attach the resolved policy to the op via a cst_id-keyed side    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā table (like the existing                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sem_model side-model) so codegen reads it. Repurpose E0096 / add policy ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā diagnostics as needed.                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā P4 ‚ÄĒ Codegen per policy                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā At each op, emit by resolved policy (replacing today's unconditional    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā check+abort):                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - index/slice !abort ‚Üí current                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā emit_bounds_check/emit_slice_bounds_check; !clamp ‚Üí min/max             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā clamp (slice) or clamped index; !zero ‚Üí in-bounds ? load : zero (skip   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā on write); !wrap ‚Üí                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā i % len.                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - insert ‚Üí !abort (current overflow-abort), !reject (no-op + sentinel), ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report (h:,ok:)                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (current mandatory-ok helper). !evict = ring cursor: pool gains one i64 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā head; on a full                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā insert do victim = head; head = (head+1) % cap; bump gen[victim] (same  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā gen-exhaustion check as                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā delete ‚ÄĒ this stales the evicted occupant's handle), overwrite          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā columns[victim], return                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (victim | gen<<32); count stays at cap, free-list untouched. O(1). ‚áí an ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict pool is for                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā anonymous streamed collectives, not rows you hold stable handles to.    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Implementation deferred                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā to a later milestone (adds the head field to the pool struct + the      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā full-path branch in the                                                 ‚Ēā

‚óŹ Done ‚ÄĒ the full plan is written to POLICY_PLAN.txt in the repo root (and it
  remains in the plan file). It captures the complete design: !policy replacing
  proc!/contagion, user-definable policy decls with core shipping the common
  ones (no special status), !abort as the sole crash source with the final-clamp
  net guaranteeing every other policy is crash-proof, ring-cursor !evict + the
  !evict_oldest TODO with pay-per-policy uses metadata, the no-unexpected-abort
  guarantee tests, and the --no-abort / --no-implicit-abort enforcement flags.

     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā Plan: failure policies (!policy) ‚ÄĒ replace proc!/contagion              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The proc! + whole-program can_panic contagion model (just built) is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā heavier than arche needs.                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā After making most things total by construction (proven indexing,        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ok-valued insert, soon-clamped                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slices), the residual set of operations that can fail at runtime is     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā tiny (~30 sites). So instead of                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā a propagation marker + call-graph effect analysis + (proposed)          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā recover/unwinding, we resolve each                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā failure locally, at the operation, by a policy ‚ÄĒ expr !policy. This     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā needs no unwinding, no                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā contagion, and gives a sharper guarantee than proc!: a func provably    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā never crashes; a proc                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā crashes only at a visible !abort site (marked at the line, not smeared  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā over the whole proc).                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ! is unified to mean "failure-handling policy" (generalizing proc!),    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā reusing the pool                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overload-policy idea from the original design discussion (Particle[100] ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā !evict).                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Locked decisions                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Replace proc! and the can_panic contagion pass entirely. Keep the     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bounds prover                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (sem_bounds* in semantic.c) and the (h:, ok:) report form. No recover / ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā no stack unwinding.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Every fallible op has a sensible DEFAULT policy (unannotated code     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā compiles); !policy                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā overrides. LSP/analyzer hints surfacing the implicit policy are         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mandatory.                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - func = total policies only (can never crash). proc may also !abort.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Slices default to !clamp; a provably-out-of-bounds constant           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slice/index is a compile error                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (don't silently clamp a statically-wrong access).                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The model                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā expr !policy attaches a deterministic failure resolution at the site.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Policies are total (op                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā cannot crash) except !abort (explicit, site-marked crash) and the (ok:) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā report form.                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ‚Ēā
